29:1194:72353:18:18:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:forward and follows that of our two-period model. Instead of (17), cumulative debt as of
29:1195:72441:18:18:72:232:285:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:B:t= 1,d, is restricted to satisfy:
29:1196:72474:18:22:258:540:267:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:A:d≤min{x, dmax}.(20)
29:1197:72493:22:18:72:536:245:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Note that borrowing is tied to out-of-pocket investment,x, and not to total investment,h.
29:1198:72582:18:18:89:539:227:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Individuals choosex≥0,c0≥0, anddto maximizeU(c0, x, d;a) subject to (20) and
29:1199:72658:18:18:72:539:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(18). Aside from the link ofdtoxinstead ofh, and the possibility ofx= 0, this problem is
29:1200:72746:18:18:72:540:191:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:analytically identical to the corresponding problem in the two-period model. Proposition 2
29:1201:72836:18:34:72:244:173:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:holds. See details in Appendix C.
29:1202:72869:34:26:72:417:139:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5.5  Private Lending with Limited Commitment
29:1203:72913:26:18:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Now, consider private loans for schooling that are subject to limited enforcement. As in the
29:1204:73005:18:0:72:540:95:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:two-period model, loans are repaid if and only if the cost of defaulting is higher than the
30:1205:73098:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cost of repaying. The incentives to repay at datest≥1 define the amount of credit lenders
30:1206:73187:18:18:72:325:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are willing to supply during the schooling period.
30:1207:73237:18:18:89:539:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We consider two penalties for default. First, defaulting borrowers are reported to credit
30:1208:73326:18:18:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bureaus, an action that is assumed to prevent the borrower from accessing formal credit
30:1209:73413:18:18:72:540:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:markets for some period. This penalty does not reduce earnings, but it disrupts the ability
30:1210:73504:18:18:72:540:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to smooth consumption and can be quite costly if labor earnings grow quickly with age or
30:1211:73592:18:18:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:if the IES is low. Second, the borrower forfeits a fractionγ∈[0,1) of his labor earnings.
30:1212:73681:18:18:72:539:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:The fractionγencompasses direct garnishments from lenders as well as the costs of actions
30:1213:73770:18:18:72:540:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:taken by the borrower to avoid direct penalties (e.g. working in the informal sector, renting
30:1214:73863:18:18:72:540:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:instead of owning a house, etc.). We assume that both penalties are active for an interval of
30:1215:73956:18:18:72:415:595:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:length 0< π < P−1 that starts the moment default takes place.34
30:1216:74019:18:18:89:539:577:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Consistent with our earlier assumptions about post-investment credit markets, we assume
30:1217:74106:18:18:72:540:559:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that loans contracted after schooling are fully enforceable and that loans contracted while
30:1218:74197:18:18:72:539:541:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in school can only be defaulted on at aget= 1. We explicitly focus on credit constraints
30:1219:74285:18:17:72:309:523:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:directly related to the financing of schooling.35
30:1220:74334:17:18:89:539:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The amount of debt that a person can credibly commit to repay depends on the discounted
30:1221:74421:18:18:72:539:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:utility associated with default. Consider a person with abilityaand human capitalhthat
30:1222:74507:18:18:72:539:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:defaults att= 1 on debtd. Since punishments are not reduced by partial re-payment, all
30:1223:74593:18:18:72:539:452:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:defaults would be on the entire debt. During the punishment period [1,1 +π], consumption
30:1224:74681:18:18:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:isc(t) = (1−γ)μ−1ahαeg(t−1). Fromt= 1 +πonwards, a fresh start allows the person
30:1225:74761:18:18:72:539:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to fully smooth consumption, including the time after retirement. The maximizedt= 1
30:1226:74844:18:31:72:531:398:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:discounted utility of a person who chooses to default at the end of the schooling period is
30:1227:74935:31:0:226:310:367:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f10:A:VD(h;a) =ˆΘγ,π
30:1228:74949:0:0:312:363:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:[μ−1aΦhα]
30:1229:74958:0:23:364:380:382:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:?:1−σ
30:1230:74961:23:0:332:360:359:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:?:1−σ
30:1231:74964:0:29:381:384:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:,
30:1232:74965:29:18:72:500:338:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:whereˆΘγ,πis a positive constant, the expression for which is shown in Appendix C.
30:1233:75047:18:18:89:539:320:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Rational lenders foresee the repayment incentives of borrowers and restrict credit to
30:1234:75132:18:18:72:539:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:avoid triggering default. Given penalties (π, γ) a borrower with abilityaand human capital
30:1235:75222:18:18:72:539:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investmenthis better off repaying a level of debtdwhenVD(h;a)≤V(h, d;a). In our
30:1236:75301:18:25:72:218:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:setting, this is equivalent to:
30:1237:75332:25:30:227:540:241:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:A:d≤κμ−1aΦ [ipub+ (1 +s)x]α,(21)
30:1238:75362:30:0:72:144:211:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:B:whereκ≡1−
30:1239:75371:0:10:146:152:224:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:?:[
30:1240:75372:10:0:154:189:214:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:ˆΘγ,π/Θ
30:1241:75379:0:13:189:209:224:12:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f18:?:]11−σ
30:1242:75384:13:18:215:539:211:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f2:A:≥0 incorporates the effects of both the garnishment and distor-
30:1243:75447:18:18:72:540:193:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tions to consumption profiles. Notice that credit limits are proportional to labor earnings,
30:1244:75539:18:18:72:539:175:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:just as we imposed in the two-period model. However, in this model, the value ofκis deter-
30:1245:75629:18:18:72:539:157:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:mined by preferences (ρ, σ) and institutions (γ, π). Below we show thatκcan be large even
30:1246:75718:18:16:72:270:139:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:if wage garnishments,γ, are negligible.
30:1247:75757:16:16:81:539:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:34Livshits, MacGee, and Tertilt (2007) make a similar set of assumptions in modelling U.S. bankruptcy
30:1248:75858:16:8:72:122:107:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:regulations.
30:1249:75870:8:0:81:539:99:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:35Monge-Naranjo (2007) considers a continuous time model in which the agent can default in any period.
31:1250:75974:0:18:89:539:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Some aspects of the determination ofκare worth mentioning. First,κis increasing in
31:1251:76056:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:B:γandπ. The option to default is less tempting with harsher punishments. Second,κ >0
31:1252:76139:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as long asπ >0, even ifγ= 0.  The exclusion from financial markets alone suffices to
31:1253:76223:18:18:72:539:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sustain lending. Third, ifπ= 0, the model boils down to an exogenous constraint model
31:1254:76308:18:18:72:444:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:withd0= 0, since no lending can be sustained in equilibrium, i.e.κ= 0.
31:1255:76378:18:18:89:539:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:With credit limits determined by limited commitment, a person chooses investment,
31:1256:76459:18:18:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:consumption and borrowing (x≥0,c0≥0 andd) to maximizeU(c0, x, d;a) subject to (18)
31:1257:76541:18:18:72:539:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and (21). Given the endogenously determinedκand ignoring the possibility ofx= 0, this
31:1258:76626:18:31:72:540:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:problem is analytically identical to the two-period case and a parallel to Proposition 3 holds.
31:1259:76721:31:18:72:539:600:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f4:F:Proposition 6Let ability and financial assets of a young individual be(a, w), and let
31:1260:76806:18:18:72:539:582:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f4:F:hL(a, w)andhU(a)indicate, respectively, the optimal investments in human capital with
31:1261:76891:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:F:private lenders with limited commitment and in the unrestricted allocation.  Ifa≤a0,
31:1262:76975:18:18:72:539:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:F:thenhL(a, w) =hU(a) =ipub.  If insteada > a0and constraint (21) binds, then: (i)
31:1263:77055:18:18:72:539:528:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f4:F:hL(a, w)< hU(a); (ii)hL(a, w)is strictly increasing inw; and (iii)hL(a, w)is strictly
31:1264:77140:18:0:72:286:510:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f2:B:increasing inaifκ≥κ(σ)≡[(σ−1)/σ]
31:1265:77172:0:10:288:293:520:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:A:[
31:1266:77173:10:0:293:348:510:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:A:(1−e−ρ)/
31:1267:77181:0:10:350:355:520:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:?:(
31:1268:77182:10:0:355:397:510:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f10:?:1−e−ρT
31:1269:77188:0:10:399:409:520:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:?:)]
31:1270:77190:10:30:409:413:510:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:.
31:1271:77191:30:18:89:539:480:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:This proposition is central to our quantitative analysis of credit constraints, given its
31:1272:77280:18:18:72:241:462:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:empirically verifiable predictions.
31:1273:77315:18:18:89:539:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Recall from our discussion in Section 4.3 that strong preferences for smooth consumption
31:1274:77403:18:18:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(i.e. a highσor low IES) generate a negative ability – investment relationship when credit
31:1275:77493:18:18:72:540:408:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraints are exogenously fixed. This tendency also exists when constraints are endogenous
31:1276:77585:18:18:72:540:390:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:since∂κ(σ)/∂σ≥0, which implies that a stronger link between investment and credit
31:1277:77666:18:18:71:540:372:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:limits (i.e. a largerκ) is needed to generate a positive ability – investment relationship as
31:1278:77759:18:18:71:539:354:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:preferences for smooth consumption become stronger.  However, a greater preference for
31:1279:77845:18:18:71:539:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:smooth consumption profiles also makes the default punishment of exclusion from credit
31:1280:77931:18:18:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:markets more painful.  Private lenders will be willing to offer more credit if the cost of
31:1281:78021:18:18:71:540:300:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:defaulting is higher. Thus,κis also increasing inσunder limited commitment. Below, we
31:1282:78106:18:18:71:540:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:show that for empirically plausible punishment parameters (γ, π) the effect ofσonκoften
31:1283:78193:18:18:72:539:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:dominates its effect onκ(σ), and a higher value ofσ(or lower IES) makes it more rather
31:1284:78279:18:17:72:540:246:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:than less likely that condition (iii) of this proposition holds. Most importantly, we show
31:1285:78369:17:18:72:539:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:thatκ > κ(σ) for empirically plausible parameters, so that the model implies a positive
31:1286:78456:18:35:72:495:211:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:relationship between investment and ability for all ability and initial wealth levels.
31:1287:78542:35:26:72:368:176:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5.6  GSL ProgramsPlusPrivate Lenders
31:1288:78578:26:18:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Finally, we consider the coexistence of a GSL program with private lenders.  As before,
31:1289:78665:18:18:72:540:132:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we assume that the repayment of loans from the GSL program is fully enforced. As noted
31:1290:78751:18:17:72:540:114:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:earlier, this assumption is in line with the fact that GSL programs in the U.S. are better
31:1291:78841:17:0:72:540:97:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:protected against default than private unsecured loans. First, private loans can be cleared
32:1292:78934:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in bankruptcy proceedings while GSL loans cannot. This implies a longer (potentially un-
32:1293:79022:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:limited) punishment period for government loans. Second, wage garnishments of up to 15%
32:1294:79109:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are explicitly incorporated in GSL programs, whereas no explicit rate exists for private un-
32:1295:79201:18:18:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:secured loans.  Third, GSL programs include a wide array of additional punishments for
32:1296:79287:18:18:72:540:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:those who default that have no counterpart in the private sector (e.g. governments can seize
32:1297:79379:18:18:72:405:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:income tax returns for those defaulting on a GSL program loan).
32:1298:79442:18:18:89:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:With both public and private sources of credit, a young person with (a, w) chooses out-of-
32:1299:79532:18:18:72:539:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:pocket investmentx, consumption during youthc0, borrowing from GSLdg, and borrowing
32:1300:79615:18:29:72:427:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from private lendersdpto maximizeU(c0, x, d;a) subject to (18) and
32:1301:79681:29:20:230:540:602:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:A:d≤dp+dg(22)
32:1302:79692:20:21:225:540:582:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:A:dp≤κμ−1aΦ [ipub+ (1 +s)x]α,(23)
32:1303:79723:21:29:225:540:561:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:A:dg≤min{x, dmax}.(24)
32:1304:79743:29:18:89:540:532:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The threshold level of initial assetswG+Lmin(a) above which individuals with abilityaare
32:1305:79831:18:18:72:540:514:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:unconstrained is given in Appendix C. As with the two-period model, this threshold is lower
32:1306:79922:18:18:72:540:496:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and fewer people are constrained than under the GSL alone or under private markets alone.
32:1307:80011:18:34:72:408:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Proposition 5 of the two-period model also applies in this setting.
32:1308:80078:34:26:72:188:444:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5.7  Calibration
32:1309:80094:26:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We now calibrate parameter values to explore the quantitative implications of the model.
32:1310:80182:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Some of the parameters are estimated using data on earnings and educational attainment
32:1311:80268:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from the random sample of males in the NLSY79. Other parameter values are calibrated
32:1312:80352:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to replicate features of the U.S. economy. We use AFQT quartiles to measure ability. All
32:1313:80440:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:dollar amounts are denominated in 1999 dollars using the Consumer Price Index (CPI-U).
32:1314:80526:18:18:72:461:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Table 3 reports the value of all parameters used in our baseline simulations.
32:1315:80603:18:17:89:539:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We assume that youth (investment period) begins at age 16 and ends at age 24. Maturity
32:1316:80689:17:18:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(labor market participation period) runs from age 24 until age 65. Retirement runs from
32:1317:80776:18:18:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:age 65 until death at age 80. Since youth lasts one period in the model, each interval of
32:1318:80865:18:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:unit length corresponds to 8 years of life. Dates for retirement and death are, respectively,
32:1319:80958:18:18:72:338:239:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:B:P= (65−16)/8 = 6.125, andT= (80−16)/8 = 8.
32:1320:81000:18:18:89:540:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To match an annual interest rate of 4%, we setρ= 8×ln(1.04) = 0.319 for the value of
32:1321:81084:18:18:72:539:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the discount rate in the model. We setσ= 2 as our baseline value to match an IES of 0.5,
32:1322:81172:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an intermediate value in the estimates in Browning, Hansen, and Heckman (1999). Values
32:1323:81258:18:18:72:331:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ofσinside the interval [1.5,3] yield similar results.
32:1324:81311:18:18:89:540:149:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Based on U.S. bankruptcy regulations, we setπ= 7/8 = 0.875 (7 year penalty period)
32:1325:81393:18:18:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as the baseline length of penalties. Also, we setγ= 0.1 for the fraction of lost earnings for
32:1326:81486:18:18:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:individuals who default. Under the GSL program guidelines, defaulting borrowers face an
32:1327:81573:18:0:72:540:95:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:explicit 15% wage garnishment. For private unsecured loans, an explicit garnishment rule

33:1343:82542:18:18:72:289:474:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to reasonable variations in this parameter.
33:1344:82585:18:18:89:539:456:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We assume all investment through age 16 is publicly provided for free. After age 16,
33:1345:82669:18:17:72:540:438:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:schooling entails direct costs (i.e. tuition and public expenditures on primary, secondary,
33:1346:82760:17:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and post-secondary schooling) and indirect costs (i.e. foregone earnings). To compute di-
33:1347:82849:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rect costs we use an annual government expenditure of $5,928 for primary and secondary
33:1348:82935:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:schooling. Annual direct expenditures for college and graduate education are assumed to
33:1349:83022:18:18:72:539:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equal $16,838.36(College expenditures include government expenditures as well as tuition
33:1350:83110:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and fees paid by students.) We setipub= $65,239, which is equal to the discounted value of
33:1351:83200:18:18:72:539:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:all direct schooling expenditures through grade nine.37This is consistent with our focus on
33:1352:83291:18:18:72:276:313:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investments made from age 16 onwards.
33:1353:83328:18:18:89:539:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Because of the laws on compulsory schooling and minimum work age, we only include
33:1354:83409:18:18:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:foregone earnings as part of investment costs for grades ten and above. To estimate foregone
33:1355:83501:18:18:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:earnings, we use data from the NLSY79 to regress log earnings on indicators for each possible
33:1356:83594:18:18:72:540:241:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:year of completed schooling from grade 10 through six years of post-secondary studies,
33:1357:83680:18:18:72:540:223:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:indicators for AFQT quartiles, total years of potential work experience and experience-
33:1358:83767:18:17:72:540:205:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:squared.38From this regression, we compute foregone earnings forS≥10 years of schooling
33:1359:83854:17:16:81:539:188:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:36Annual expenditure for education through grade twelve (for college and graduate education) is the
33:1360:83953:16:12:72:540:172:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:average of annual current expenditures per pupil for public primary and secondary schools (for all two
33:1361:84055:12:12:72:540:160:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and four year colleges) over the academic years 1979-80 through 1988-89 as reported in Table 170 (Table
33:1362:84158:12:12:72:539:148:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:342) of theDigest of Education Statistics, 1999. These years roughly reflect the years our NLSY79 sample
33:1363:84262:12:8:72:284:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:respondents made their final schooling decisions.
33:1364:84311:8:16:81:539:128:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:37We use a 4% annual discount rate, reporting the value discounted to the end of grade nine. Less than
33:1365:84413:16:8:72:360:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:0.2% of our NLSY79 sample acquired less than 10 years of school.
33:1366:84477:8:0:81:539:104:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:38This regression uses all available earnings observations for male respondents with at least nine years of
34:1367:84586:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:using the predicted earnings of someone with nine years of completed schooling,S−10
34:1368:84669:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:years of potential work experience, and the desired AFQT quartile. These foregone earnings
34:1369:84759:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:estimates are included in our estimates of total schooling expenditures and are reported in
34:1370:84850:18:18:72:209:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Table D1 of the Appendix.
34:1371:84875:18:18:89:540:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We calibrate the government subsidy ratesas follows.  We assume that the private

34:1395:86725:18:18:72:488:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the most able are on average about 50% more productive than are the least able.
34:1396:86804:18:18:89:539:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Ideally, we would like to specify a joint distribution of wealth and ability to simulate our
34:1397:86896:18:17:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model and compute the distribution of investment in the economy. Unfortunately, this is
34:1398:86983:17:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:not feasible. We do not directly observe the assets available to youth, because they not only
34:1399:87076:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:depend on their parents net worth and income but also on intra-family transfers, which are
34:1400:87166:18:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:not always observed. Modelling these transfers is beyond the scope of this paper. Instead, we
34:1401:87259:18:18:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:analyze investment behavior for our estimated ability types and a range of potential wealth
34:1402:87350:18:22:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:levels. While we cannot compare moments for investment implied by the model with those
34:1403:87436:22:12:72:540:137:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:completed schooling when they were ages 16-24 and no longer enrolled in school. Potential work experience
34:1404:87541:12:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:is measured as age - years of completed schooling - 6. The estimates (available upon request) suggest that
34:1405:87647:12:12:72:540:113:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:earnings for these young workers are generally increasing in years of completed schooling and increasing and
34:1406:87755:12:0:72:235:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:concave in potential work experience.
35:1407:87794:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:observed in the data, we can explore whether investment is increasing in ability and wealth
35:1408:87885:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:over reasonable ranges of wealth, how investment behavior depends on the type of constraints
35:1409:87977:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we assume, and how investment and borrowing (as functions of ability and wealth) respond
35:1410:88065:18:18:72:210:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to changes in the economy.
35:1411:88091:18:18:89:539:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Because foregone earnings are an important part of investment expenditures in our cal-
35:1412:88177:18:18:72:539:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ibration, an individual’s initial wealth,w, includes at least the amount he could earn if he
35:1413:88269:18:18:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:left school after grade 9 and began working. This amount depends on ability, since foregone
35:1414:88360:18:18:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:earnings depend on ability (see Appendix Table D1). The relevant range of initial wealth,
35:1415:88449:18:18:72:540:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:therefore, begins at $52,000 for the least able, $74,000 for AFQT quartile 2, and $80–84,000
35:1416:88541:18:18:72:540:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for the top two quartiles. Any wealth levels above these amounts must come from parents
35:1417:88628:18:34:72:197:595:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:or other outside sources.
35:1418:88653:34:26:72:254:561:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5.8  Baseline Simulations
35:1419:88678:26:18:72:540:535:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We are primarily interested in the implied cross-sectional relationship between ability, wealth,
35:1420:88774:18:18:72:540:517:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and investment in our model with both the GSL and private lenders.  We begin with a
35:1421:88857:18:18:72:540:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:discussion of borrowing constraints in this environment and then discuss investment behavior.
35:1422:88950:18:18:89:539:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 5 shows a very strong result: for any value ofσ≥0, the limited commitment
35:1423:89030:18:18:72:540:463:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model implies a positive relationship between investment and ability given our values for

35:1427:89376:18:18:71:539:391:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:B:γandπ. The figure also displaysκ(σ) as defined in Proposition 6 (dashed line). When

35:1429:89546:17:18:71:539:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:our baseline parameters.  This is also true if the only penalty for default is a seven-year
35:1430:89637:18:18:71:540:338:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:exclusion from financial markets (π= 7/8, γ= 0) or if the exclusion period lasts only one

35:1433:89896:18:18:72:508:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is only a positive relationship between ability and investment if 0≤σ <1 (IES>1).
35:1434:89977:18:18:89:539:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:As discussed earlier, bothκandκ(σ) are increasing inσ. Over most of the empirically
35:1435:90060:18:18:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:relevant range whereσ >1 (IES<1), an increase inσmakes it more rather than less likely
35:1436:90146:18:18:72:487:230:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the condition in Proposition 6 is met and investment is increasing in ability.
35:1437:90229:18:18:89:539:212:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 6 shows the implied borrowing constraints as a function of individual investment

35:1440:90500:18:18:72:540:158:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:While offering sizeable loans to students, private lenders do not offer as much as the GSL
35:1441:90590:18:18:72:540:140:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:program over a wide range of investment amounts. At any level of investment, the difference

36:1465:91481:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:source is exhausted, they may borrow from private lenders. As one can see, our calibrated
36:1466:91570:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model implies that private borrowing should be negligible during the baseline period (i.e. for
36:1467:91664:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:NLSY79 cohorts). As noted earlier, initial assets for all individuals are at least as high as the
36:1468:91761:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:potential earnings they would receive if they quit school after grade 9: $52,000 for the lowest
36:1469:91856:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:AFQT quartile, $74,000 for the second lowest, and $80–84,000 for the top two quartiles. For
36:1470:91947:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:all ability quartiles, borrowing from private lenders is zero for asset levels above potential
36:1471:92041:18:17:72:189:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:school-period earnings.
36:1472:92064:17:18:89:539:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:For all ability types, individuals with initial assets above $40,000 (far below potential
36:1473:92153:18:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:school-period earnings) invest the unconstrained optimal amounts. As a result, investment
36:1474:92242:18:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is increasing in ability and independent of initial assets, consistent with reported schooling
36:1475:92336:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:patterns in the NLSY79 data. Optimal total human capital investment ranges from roughly
36:1476:92423:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:$85,000 for the least able to $130,000 for the second ability quartile to around $165,000 for
36:1477:92516:18:18:72:226:149:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:the top two ability quartiles.40
36:1478:92548:18:16:81:539:131:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:40With private lending markets alone, the most able are constrained up through initial asset levels of
36:1479:92650:16:11:72:540:115:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:around $85,000. With the GSL alone or with exogenous constraints, the most able are constrained through
36:1480:92753:11:0:72:540:104:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:initial asset levels of around $70,000. In all cases, investment is unconstrained for asset levels above potential

38:1523:93251:0:18:89:539:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It is noteworthy that the investment amounts implied by the model are fairly close to
38:1524:93336:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:average total expenditures by AFQT quartile in the NLSY79 data, even though we did not
38:1525:93422:18:18:72:539:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:target these values.41This external validity provides additional confidence in our model and
38:1526:93514:18:35:72:226:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the baseline parameterization.
38:1527:93544:35:26:72:451:686:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5.9  A Rise in the Costs of and Returns to Schooling
38:1528:93596:26:18:72:540:660:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We now simulate the effects of an increase in the costs of and returns to schooling — two
38:1529:93685:18:17:72:540:642:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:major economic changes that took place between the early 1980s and early 2000s.  We
38:1530:93768:17:18:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:aim to see whether the model can reproduce the observed rise in private lending as well
38:1531:93855:18:18:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as the increased effects of family income on educational attainment. We also compare the
38:1532:93943:18:18:72:540:589:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investment and consumption allocations under different assumptions about credit markets.
38:1533:94031:18:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This sheds light on the importance of a GSL program for investment, as well as the role
38:1534:94118:18:18:72:540:553:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:played by private lenders today. We also compare these environments with the standard
38:1535:94203:18:18:72:378:535:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model, which assumes borrowing constraints are exogenous.
38:1536:94260:18:18:89:539:517:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We model an increase in the wage returns to education by assuming thatαincreases
38:1537:94340:18:18:72:540:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by 0.02 (from the baseline estimate of 0.432).  This change produces a modest increase
38:1538:94426:18:18:72:540:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the college – high school log wage differential. We model the rise in net tuition costs by
38:1539:94519:18:18:72:539:463:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assuming that the government subsidy rate,s, falls from 1.19 to 1.05. This reduction reflects
38:1540:94612:18:18:72:540:445:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the increased importance of tuition and fees as a fraction of total current-fund revenue for
38:1541:94704:18:18:72:540:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:public and private universities in the U.S. Finally, we incorporate the stability of maximum
38:1542:94796:18:18:72:435:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:GSL loan limits by assuming thatdmaxremains unchanged at $35,000.
38:1543:94861:18:18:89:539:391:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 8 graphs the new private lending limits against the unchanged GSL limits. For
38:1544:94945:18:17:72:540:373:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:all investment and ability levels, private credit limits increase by at least $3,000 over the
38:1545:95038:17:18:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:baseline amounts, with much larger increases at higher investment amounts. This increase
38:1546:95126:18:18:72:540:338:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is entirely driven by the increased return to investment, which raises the monetary costs of
38:1547:95218:18:18:72:407:320:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:default and, therefore, the amount students can commit to repay.
38:1548:95282:18:18:89:539:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Youth wish to borrow more in response to increases in the costs and returns to investment.
38:1549:95372:18:18:72:540:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:With no increase in credit available from the GSL, private lenders must cover the increased
38:1550:95463:18:18:72:540:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand for credit. Indeed, Figure 9 shows that private lending increases substantially. While
38:1551:95556:18:18:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the least able youth still do not borrow from private lenders, high ability youth with low
38:1552:95646:18:18:72:298:230:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:asset levels now borrow as much as $50,000.
38:1553:95689:18:18:89:539:212:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 10 shows investment behavior under the higher assumed costs and returns to
38:1554:95770:18:18:72:539:194:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:school (i.e.α= 0.453 ands= 1.05) for the four different models of credit constraints
38:1555:95854:18:18:71:539:176:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(GSL plus private lenders, private lenders alone, GSL alone, and exogenous constraints with
38:1556:95945:18:22:71:539:158:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f2:B:d0=dmax). First, panel (a) considers investment in our preferred model with a GSL program
38:1557:96034:22:8:72:172:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:school-period earnings.
38:1558:96057:8:16:81:539:128:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:41Combining the total costs by AFQT quartile and schooling level reported in Table D1 with the distri-
38:1559:96159:16:12:72:540:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:bution of educational attainment by AFQT in the NLSY79, we obtain average total investment amounts

40:1606:96706:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and private lending. Investment increases noticeably relative to the baseline economy. This
40:1607:96797:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increase would have been even greater if private costs had not risen as well.  Borrowing
40:1608:96885:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraints now appear to be binding for a broad range of initial asset levels among the
40:1609:96973:18:18:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:higher ability types. Individuals in the top two ability quartiles with assets below $100,000
40:1610:97066:18:18:72:540:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:($15-20 thousand above potential school-period earnings) are constrained. Individuals in the
40:1611:97158:18:18:72:540:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:second lowest ability quartile with initial assets below $60,000 (less than potential school-
40:1612:97251:18:18:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:period earnings) are constrained. The least able are unconstrained for all reported levels of
40:1613:97344:18:18:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:wealth. Consistent with the NLSY97 data, family resources have become more important
40:1614:97428:18:18:72:330:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for investment among a broader set of individuals.
40:1615:97478:18:18:89:539:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Now, contemplate eliminating either source of credit. Panel (b) of Figure 10 considers
40:1616:97564:18:18:72:540:595:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:private lending alone, while panel (c) considers the GSL program alone.  In both cases,
40:1617:97651:18:18:72:540:577:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:individuals from a much broader range of initial assets and abilities are constrained and
40:1618:97740:18:18:72:540:559:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:invest less than in panel (a) when both sources are present. For most initial asset and ability
40:1619:97835:18:18:72:540:541:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:levels, the private lending market and GSL yield fairly similar investment levels; however,
40:1620:97926:18:17:72:540:523:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this is not true for those with very low initial assets (amounts below potential school-period
40:1621:98020:17:18:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:earnings). Under the GSL, these youth would invest the maximum amount they can borrow,
40:1622:98106:18:18:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:$35,000, above the publicly provided amount. Investing less does not provide them with any
40:1623:98196:18:18:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:more consumption while in school, since they would also be required to borrow less. Private
40:1624:98287:18:18:72:540:452:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:lenders do not impose this tight restriction, so very poor youth would invest less even though
40:1625:98381:18:18:72:354:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:they may be able to borrow more than under the GSL.
40:1626:98432:18:18:89:539:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Notice that both models which incorporate private lending (panels a and b) imply a posi-
40:1627:98520:18:18:72:540:398:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tive relationship between ability and investment for all levels of assets; although, investment
40:1628:98615:18:18:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is quite similar across ability types for very low asset levels (below potential school-period
40:1629:98709:18:18:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:earnings). This is not the case for the GSL alone (panel c), since the upper limit on borrow-
40:1630:98802:18:18:72:540:344:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ing is the binding constraint for a broad range of initial asset levels and ability types. The
40:1631:98896:18:18:72:540:326:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:perverse relationship between ability and optimal investment is even worse for the exogenous
40:1632:98988:18:18:72:275:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraint model as shown in panel (d).
40:1633:99027:18:18:89:539:290:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, we show consumption during the investment period under all four credit market
40:1634:99113:18:18:72:540:272:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assumptions in Figure 11. Consumption is substantially higher when both the GSL and pri-
40:1635:99201:18:17:72:540:254:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:vate lending markets are available than when either is not. As expected from our discussion
40:1636:99292:17:18:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the GSL program in Section 4, consumption while in school is quite low for those with
40:1637:99380:18:18:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:low initial assets. The fact that borrowing cannot be used to finance consumption under the
40:1638:99471:18:18:72:540:201:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:GSL can be quite costly for the poor in the absence of private lending. All other forms of
40:1639:99561:18:18:72:540:183:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:credit constraints allow for more intertemporal consumption smoothing, even if it is at the
40:1640:99652:18:0:72:218:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:expense of lower investment.

42:1793:100846:9:0:361:383:354:3:Helvetica:3:Helvetica:?:a4 (high)
43:1794:100857:0:30:72:201:775:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:C:6  Conclusions
43:1795:100871:30:18:72:540:745:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This paper develops a lifecycle human capital investment model that incorporates the bor-
43:1796:100960:18:18:72:540:727:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rowing opportunities of GSL programs and private lenders who face limited commitment by
43:1797:101047:18:18:72:540:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:borrowers. Both types of lenders directly link credit to investment behavior, with private
43:1798:101137:18:18:72:540:691:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:lenders further linking credit to observable borrower characteristics that determine invest-
43:1799:101229:18:18:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ment productivity. These links are absent in previous models and we show that they play a
43:1800:101318:18:18:72:396:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central role in determining human capital investment behavior.
43:1801:101380:18:18:89:539:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We draw three broad lessons. First, our model with endogenous borrowing constraints is
43:1802:101466:18:18:72:540:619:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:consistent with empirical studies in that it implies positive effects of both family income and
43:1803:101561:18:18:72:540:601:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ability on schooling attainment among constrained borrowers. In contrast, under empirically
43:1804:101652:18:18:72:540:583:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:plausible assumptions, a standard exogenous constraint model predicts a negative ability –
43:1805:101742:18:18:72:540:565:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:schooling relationship for constrained borrowers. Second, the direct link between credit and
43:1806:101834:18:17:72:540:547:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investment inherent in GSL programs breaks the tradeoff between income maximization and
43:1807:101921:17:18:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:consumption smoothing for some constrained borrowers. As a result, students constrained
43:1808:102008:18:18:72:540:512:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by GSL limits from borrowing more then they invest will choose to invest the unconstrained
43:1809:102098:18:18:72:540:494:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:optimal amount.  Previous empirical tests based only on educational attainment (or the
43:1810:102184:18:18:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:marginal returns on investment) cannot detect this constraint. Third, our model is able to
43:1811:102274:18:18:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reproduce the increased effect of family income on college attendance, the increased fraction
43:1812:102367:18:18:72:540:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of students borrowing the maximum amount from GSL programs, and the increased student
43:1813:102452:18:18:72:540:422:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing from private lenders over the last few decades as an equilibrium response to rising
43:1814:102545:18:18:72:201:404:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:college costs and returns.
43:1815:102571:18:18:89:539:386:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It is important to consider both GSL programs and private lenders when modelling hu-
43:1816:102655:18:18:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:man capital investment decisions. The features of GSL programs allow for the possibility
43:1817:102743:18:18:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that some student borrowers invest the optimal unconstrained amount even if they are con-
43:1818:102832:18:18:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:strained. For them, the existence of a private loan market allows for better smoothing of
43:1819:102921:18:18:72:540:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:consumption over time. The presence of private lending generates a positive relationship
43:1820:103009:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:between ability and investment for individuals from all income backgrounds – a robust em-
43:1821:103098:18:17:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:pirical pattern. The co-existence of private and public sources of credit yields some important
43:1822:103193:17:18:72:540:261:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interactions. First and foremost, investment is higher when both sources are available than
43:1823:103284:18:18:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:when only one or the other exists. Our quantitative analysis suggests that many more per-
43:1824:103373:18:18:72:540:225:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sons would be constrained in the absence of either GSL programs or a private student loan
43:1825:103462:18:18:72:540:207:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:market. We also show that private loan limits should depend positively on the better en-
43:1826:103550:18:18:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:forced GSL credit limits. An increase in GSL loan limits may crowd out some borrowing
43:1827:103635:18:18:72:463:171:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from private lenders, but it will not cause private lenders to offer less credit.
43:1828:103716:18:18:89:539:153:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We use an analytically tractable model to show that the main features of GSL programs
43:1829:103801:18:18:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and private lending under limited commitment are important for explaining observed in-
43:1830:103887:18:18:72:540:117:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:vestment patterns. An obvious next step is to introduce uncertainty about the returns to
43:1831:103975:18:0:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investment. While we do not expect such an extension to alter our predictions about the
44:1832:104064:0:18:72:540:775:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:relationship between investment, ability and family resources in any important way, incor-
44:1833:104154:18:18:72:540:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:porating uncertainty opens new and interesting areas of inquiry. With uncertainty about
44:1834:104241:18:18:72:540:739:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:labor market success, the option of default provides insurance against adverse outcomes.
44:1835:104329:18:18:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Private lenders and governments must strike a balance between providing this insurance to
44:1836:104418:18:18:72:540:703:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:borrowers and enforcing repayment. This defines an interesting optimal lending and enforce-
44:1837:104509:18:18:72:540:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ment policy, which may be complicated by the fact that students possess private information
44:1838:104600:18:18:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:about their own abilities or willingness to study. Additionally, the existence of labor market
44:1839:104694:18:18:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:uncertainty generally implies default by some agents in equilibrium. This makes it possible
44:1840:104785:18:18:72:540:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to study which agents are most likely to default and how economic changes and public poli-
44:1841:104875:18:18:72:540:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cies affect default behavior. We view our framework as a natural starting point for these
44:1842:104964:18:18:72:160:595:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:types of analysis.
44:1843:104982:18:18:89:539:577:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We also suggest that future empirical efforts to estimate school-choice models consider
44:1844:105069:18:18:72:540:559:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the types of endogenous constraints and punishments we emphasize here.  With reliable
44:1845:105154:18:18:72:540:541:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:data on schooling, borrowing, earnings, and loan repayment (an admittedly tall order),
44:1846:105240:18:17:72:540:523:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:structural estimation may be able to identify more general punishment strategies than we
44:1847:105328:17:18:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have assumed in this paper. Such an analysis would provide important new insights about
44:1848:105415:18:18:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the role of borrowing constraints, who is likely to be constrained, and how higher education
44:1849:105507:18:0:72:439:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policies and economic changes affect schooling and borrowing decisions.
45:1850:105580:0:33:72:169:775:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:C:Appendices
45:1851:105590:33:27:72:347:742:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:C:A   NLSY79 and NLSY97 Data
45:1852:105616:27:16:72:540:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:The NLSY79 is a random survey of American youth ages 14-21 at the beginning of 1979, while the
45:1853:105710:16:16:72:540:699:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:NLSY97 samples youth ages 12-16 at the beginning of 1997.42Since the oldest respondents in the
45:1854:105804:16:16:72:540:683:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:NLSY97 recently turned age 24 in the 2004 wave of data, we analyze college attendance as of age
45:1855:105899:16:16:72:165:667:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:21 in both samples.
45:1856:105918:16:16:89:539:651:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:Individuals are considered to have attended college if theyattendedat least 13 years of school
45:1857:106012:16:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:by the age of 21.43For the 1979 cohort, we use average family income when youth are ages 16-17,
45:1858:106107:16:16:71:539:619:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:excluding those not living with their parents at these ages. In the NLSY97 data, we use household
45:1859:106204:16:15:71:539:603:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:income and net wealth reported in 1997 (corresponding to ages 13-17), dropping individuals not
45:1860:106298:15:16:71:540:588:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:living with their parents that year.44We use AFQT as a measure of cognitive ability.  It is a
45:1861:106391:16:16:72:540:572:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:composite score from four subtests of the Armed Services Vocational Aptitude Battery (ASVAB)
45:1862:106483:16:16:72:540:556:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:used by the U.S. military: arithmetic reasoning, word knowledge, paragraph comprehension, and
45:1863:106576:16:16:72:540:540:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:numerical operations.  These tests are taken by respondents in both the NLSY79 and NLSY97
45:1864:106665:16:16:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:during their teenage years as part of the survey process. We categorize individuals according to
45:1865:106761:16:16:72:462:508:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f3:F:their family income, family net wealth (in NLSY97), and AFQT score quartiles.45
45:1866:106840:16:16:89:540:492:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:Our multivariate analysis controls for a host of family background variables. For both cohorts,
45:1867:106935:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:we control for maternal education by categorizing mothers as high school dropouts, those who
45:1868:107027:16:16:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:completed high school or more, and those who completed at least one year of college. We account
45:1869:107122:16:16:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:for family structure in the NLSY79 by controlling for the number of siblings the youth reported in
45:1870:107220:16:16:72:540:428:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:1979. For the NLSY97, we control for the number of household members under the age of 18 as of
45:1871:107314:16:16:72:540:412:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:the 1997 survey date. Additional family structure information is provided by an indicator variable
45:1872:107412:16:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:for whether both parents are present in the home at age 14 in the NLSY79 and in 1997 (i.e. ages
45:1873:107507:16:16:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:13-17) in the NLSY97. Family residence in an urban (metropolitan) area at age 14 (age 12) is
45:1874:107599:16:16:72:540:364:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:accounted for with the 1979 (1997) cohort. We control for the mother’s age at birth as well as
45:1875:107693:16:16:72:540:348:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:gender and race (blacks, hispanics and whites for the NLSY79; blacks, hispanics, other non-whites,
45:1876:107791:16:38:72:471:332:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:and whites for the NLSY97 data). Finally, we allow for differences by year of birth.
45:1877:107875:38:29:72:540:294:17:g_d0_f1:17:g_d0_f1:F:B  Proofs and Other Aspects of the Two-Period Model
45:1878:107926:29:23:72:352:265:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:B.1  The set of constrained individuals
45:1879:107965:23:16:72:540:242:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:For each ability levela, the various forms of credit constraints define a threshold wealth level below
45:1880:108067:16:18:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F:which the agent is constrained (and above which he is not). We now characterize those thresholds.
45:1881:108164:18:12:81:526:208:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:?:42See Belley and Lochner (2007) for additional details on the sample and variables used in this paper.
45:1882:108266:12:15:81:539:196:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:43Schooling attainment by age 22 is used if it is missing or unavailable at age 21 (fewer than 10% of all
45:1883:108371:15:9:72:201:181:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:respondents in both surveys).
45:1884:108400:9:15:81:539:172:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:44Family income includes government transfers (e.g. welfare and unemployment insurance), but it does
45:1885:108500:15:12:72:540:157:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:not subtract taxes. Net wealth measures the value of all assets (e.g. home and other real estate, vehicles,
45:1886:108607:12:9:72:441:145:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:checking and savings, and other financial assets) less any loans and credit card debt.
45:1887:108693:9:15:81:539:136:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:45Since AFQT percentile scores increase with age in the NLSY79, we determine an individual’s quartile
45:1888:108794:15:12:72:540:121:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:based on year of birth. AFQT percentile scores in the NLSY97 have already been adjusted to account for
45:1889:108896:12:0:72:138:109:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:age differences.
